2:20:1010:0:13:71:498:694:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Information Dynamics and Equilibrium Multiplicity in Global Games of Regime Change
2:21:1092:13:12:71:399:681:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:George-Marios Angeletos, Christian Hellwig, and Alessandro Pavan
2:22:1156:12:13:71:232:669:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:NBER Working Paper No. 11017
2:23:1184:13:13:71:147:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:December 2004
2:24:1197:13:27:71:188:643:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:JEL No. C7, D7, D8, F3
2:25:1219:27:31:273:338:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:?:ABSTRACT
2:26:1227:31:24:71:539:585:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Global games of regime change –  that is, coordination games of incomplete information in which
2:27:1322:24:24:71:539:561:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:a status quo is abandoned once a sufficiently large fraction of agents attacks it – have been used to
2:28:1423:24:24:71:539:537:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:study crises phenomena such as currency attacks, bank runs, debt crises, and political change. We
2:29:1520:24:24:71:539:513:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:extend the static benchmark examined in the literature by allowing agents to accumulate information
2:30:1619:24:24:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:over time and take actions in many periods. It is shown that dynamics may lead to multiple equilibria
2:31:1720:24:24:71:539:465:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:under  the  same  information  assumptions  that  guarantee  uniqueness  in  the  static  benchmark.
2:32:1820:24:24:71:539:441:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Multiplicity  originates  in  the  interaction  between  the  arrival  of  information  over  time  and  the
2:33:1928:24:24:71:539:417:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:endogenous change in beliefs induced by the knowledge that the regime survived past attacks. This
2:34:2025:24:24:71:539:393:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:interaction also generates interesting equilibrium properties, such as the possibility that fundamentals
2:35:2129:24:24:71:539:369:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:predict the eventual regime outcome but not the timing or the number of attacks, or that dynamics
2:36:2226:24:31:71:470:345:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:alternate between crises and phases of tranquility without changes in fundamentals.
2:37:2309:31:14:71:198:314:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:George -Marios Angeletos
2:38:2333:14:14:71:197:300:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Department of Economics
2:39:2356:14:14:71:93:286:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:MIT
2:40:2359:14:15:71:211:272:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:50 Memorial Drive, E51-251
2:41:2385:15:14:71:182:257:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Cambridge, MA 02142
2:42:2404:14:14:71:123:243:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and NBER
2:43:2412:14:28:71:153:229:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:angelet@mit.edu
2:44:2427:28:14:71:157:201:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Christian Hellwig
2:45:2444:14:15:71:103:187:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:UCLA
2:46:2448:15:28:71:171:172:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:chris@econ.ucla.edu
2:47:2467:28:14:71:157:144:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Alessandro Pavan
2:48:2483:14:14:71:190:130:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Northwestern University
2:49:2506:14:0:71:207:116:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:alepavan@northwestern.edu
3:50:2531:0:30:72:201:709:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:C:1Introduction
3:51:2544:30:18:72:540:679:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Coordination games in which a status quo is abandoned once a sufficiently large number of agents
3:52:2640:18:18:72:540:661:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:takes an action that favors regime change  have been used to study a variety of socioeconomic
3:53:2733:18:17:72:539:643:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:phenomena. Whereas the earlier contributions in the literature focused on the existence and im-
3:54:2828:17:18:72:540:626:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:plications of multiple equilibria when agents can perfectly coordinate with each other, recent work
3:55:2927:18:17:72:540:608:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:on global games by Carlsson and van Damme (1993) and Morris and Shin (1998, 2000, 2001)
3:56:3014:17:18:72:540:591:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:has emphasized the fragility of this multiplicity to perturbations of the information structure away
3:57:3114:18:18:72:539:573:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:from common knowledge: a unique equilibrium often survives when agents observe a payoff-relevant
3:58:3210:18:18:71:446:555:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:variable, such as the strength of the status quo, with small idiosyncratic noise.
3:59:3291:18:18:91:539:537:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Variants of this uniqueness result have been established in the context of currency crises, bank
3:60:3387:18:17:71:539:519:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:runs, debt crises, and political change.1Most of this work assumes a static coordination game, thus
3:61:3486:17:18:71:539:502:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:abstracting from the possibility that agents may have the option to take multiple shots against the
3:62:3585:18:19:71:496:484:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:regime. For many of the applications of interest, however, this possibility seems relevant.
3:63:3676:19:17:91:539:465:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:In this paper, we extend the static benchmark examined in the literature by allowing agents
3:64:3767:17:18:71:539:448:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:to take actions in multiple periods and accumulate information over time. There is a large number
3:65:3864:18:17:71:539:430:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of agents and two possible regimes, the status quo and an alternative. In any given period, each
3:66:3960:17:18:71:539:413:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:agent has a binary choice: he may either “attack” the status quo (that is, take an action that favors
3:67:4061:18:18:71:539:395:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:regime change) or “not attack”. Attacking is individually optimal if and only if the probability of
3:68:4160:18:17:71:539:377:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:regime change in that period is sufficiently high. The status quo, in turn, is abandoned if and only
3:69:4260:17:18:71:539:360:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:if the fraction of agents attacking exceeds a critical valueθ∈R,which parametrizes the strength of
3:70:4358:18:18:71:540:342:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the status quo.θis the component of the payoffstructure — commonly referred to as the exogenous
3:71:4453:18:17:71:539:324:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:fundamentals — which is never common knowledge among the agents.  Instead, as time passes,
3:72:4543:17:19:71:281:307:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:agents receive noisy private signals aboutθ.
3:73:4587:19:17:91:540:288:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:We show that dynamics may sustain multiple equilibria under the same information assump-
3:74:4675:17:18:71:539:271:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:tions that guarantee uniqueness in the static benchmark, namely that the precision of the agents’
3:75:4772:18:18:71:539:253:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:private information is sufficiently high relative to the precision of the initial common prior. Multi-
3:76:4874:18:17:71:539:235:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:plicity originates in the interaction between two elements: the knowledge that the regime survived
3:77:4972:17:19:71:385:218:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:past attacks and the arrival of new private information over time.
3:78:5038:19:17:91:539:199:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:In thefirst period, agentsfind it dominant to attack for sufficiently low realizations of their
3:79:5133:17:18:71:539:182:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:private signals. This ensures that, in any equilibrium, regime change takes place in thefirst period
3:80:5233:18:18:71:539:164:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:for sufficiently lowθ.At any future date, the observation that the status quo is still in place makes
3:81:5334:18:17:71:540:146:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:it common certainty that it is not too weak, for otherwise it would have collapsed under thefirst
3:82:5431:17:18:72:105:129:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:attack.
3:83:5438:18:18:84:540:111:36:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:1See Morris and Shin (1998) for currency crises; Goldstein and Pauzner (2000) and Rochet and Vives (2004) for
3:84:5547:18:14:71:539:93:82:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:bank runs; Morris and Shin (2004) and Corsetti, Guimaraes and Roubini (2004) for debt crises; Chamley (1999) for
3:85:5659:14:0:71:406:79:82:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:regime switches; Atkeson (2000) and Edmond (2004) for riots and political change.
4:86:5741:0:18:91:539:709:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:This effect implies that no agent is willing to attackin any subsequent period if he expects no
4:87:5836:18:17:71:539:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:other agent to attack. Hence, there always exists an equilibrium in which no attack occurs after
4:88:5932:17:18:71:540:674:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:thefirst period. In fact, if no new information wereto arrive over time, this would be the unique
4:89:6029:18:18:71:540:656:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrium of the game. The possibility to takemultiple shots against the regime would then add
4:90:6125:18:22:71:213:638:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:nothing to the static analysis.
4:91:6156:22:17:91:540:616:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:However, as agents receive new private signals aboutθ, the impact of the knowledge that the
4:92:6247:17:18:71:539:599:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:regime survived past attacks on posterior beliefs eventually vanishes. For the same reason, the
4:93:6342:18:18:71:540:581:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:dependence of posterior beliefs on the initial common prior also diminishes over time. When the
4:94:6437:18:17:71:539:563:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:prior is relatively aggressive, in the sense that it induces a large attack in thefirst period, the
4:95:6536:17:18:71:539:546:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:increase in the precision of private information would induce less aggressive behavior even in the
4:96:6634:18:17:71:540:528:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:absence of past attacks. In this case, no action after thefirst period remains the unique equilibrium.
4:97:6736:17:18:71:540:511:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:In contrast, when the prior is relatively lenient, both the discounting of the prior and the discounting
4:98:6840:18:18:71:539:493:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of the knowledge that the regime survived past attacks contribute to making new attacks eventually
4:99:6938:18:17:71:540:475:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:possible. Hence, there also exist equilibria where agents take multiple shots against the regime.
4:100:7035:17:18:71:540:458:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Indeed, we show that, unless the game ends for exogenous reasons infinite time, any arbitrary
4:101:7128:18:22:72:315:440:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:number of attacks can be sustained in equilibrium.
4:102:7178:22:18:91:539:418:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:In the benchmark model, we deliberately assume away the possibility that the critical size
4:103:7268:18:17:72:540:400:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of attack necessary for regime change varies over time.  This allows us to isolate the effects of
4:104:7365:17:18:72:540:383:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:changes in information, as opposed to changes in fundamentals, on the dynamics of coordination.
4:105:7460:18:17:72:540:365:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Nevertheless, we also show that the multiplicity result is robust to the introduction of shocks to
4:106:7558:17:18:72:540:348:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the fundamentals — in which case dominant actions may exist in every period — provided that the
4:107:7653:18:18:72:540:330:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:volatility of these shocks is sufficiently small. In the limit, as the volatility vanishes, any equilibrium
4:108:7760:18:17:72:539:312:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of the benchmark model can be approximated arbitrarily closely by an equilibrium in the game
4:109:7852:17:18:72:540:295:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:with shocks. What sustains the multiplicity ofequilibria and the corresponding dynamics is again
4:110:7948:18:17:72:540:277:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the combination of the arrival of new information over time with the endogenous upward shift
4:111:8040:17:18:72:540:260:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:in posterior beliefs that follows from the knowledge that the regime survived past attacks. That
4:112:8136:18:18:72:539:242:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:this shift takes the form of a truncation in the benchmark model simplifies the construction of the
4:113:8235:18:22:72:367:224:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrium set, but is not essential for the multiplicity result.
4:114:8301:22:17:91:539:202:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:We also emphasize that multiplicity does not originate from the presence of exogenous public
4:115:8393:17:18:72:540:185:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:signals or the observation of the size of past attacks. Indeed, for most of the analysis we assume
4:116:8491:18:18:72:540:167:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:away any such source of information and concentrate on the case in which agents receive only
4:117:8583:18:17:72:540:149:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:private signals over time.  What the introduction of public news does, is to “smooth out” the
4:118:8676:17:18:72:540:132:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:dependence of the determinacy of equilibria on the initial prior: multiple equilibria then exist
4:119:8772:18:17:72:540:114:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:whatever the horizon of the game and for any prior mean and any relative precision of public and
4:120:8868:17:18:72:540:97:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:private information.  Finally, introducing endogenous signals about the size of past attacks — a
4:121:8964:18:0:72:540:79:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:simple form of (noisy) social learning — does not change the equilibrium dynamics, except for the
5:122:9062:0:18:72:540:709:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:possibility that the endogenous information revealed by the size of an attack may substitute for
5:123:9158:18:17:72:540:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the arrival of new exogenous information and render further attacks possible immediately after an
5:124:9255:17:19:72:153:674:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:unsuccessful one.
5:125:9272:19:18:91:539:655:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:The existence of multiple equilibria leads todynamics that might not have been possible with
5:126:9364:18:17:71:540:637:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:either common knowledge or a unique equilibrium.  For example, fundamentals may determine
5:127:9453:17:18:71:539:620:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:thefinal regime outcome (e.g., whether a currency is eventually devalued) but not the timing and
5:128:9549:18:17:71:539:602:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:number of attacks. Moreover, dynamics may take the form of sequences of periods in which attacks
5:129:9645:17:18:71:539:585:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:can not occur and agents only accumulate information, followed by periods in which an attack is
5:130:9740:18:18:71:539:567:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:possible but does not take place, eventually resulting in a new attack. An economy can thus transit
5:131:9839:18:18:71:537:549:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:from phases of tranquility to criseswithoutany change in the underlying economic fundamentals.
5:132:9933:18:18:91:539:531:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Below, we discuss the relation of the paper to the pertinent literature. Section 2 then reviews the
5:133:10032:18:17:72:540:513:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:static benchmark and introduces the dynamic model. Section 3 characterizes the set of monotone
5:134:10126:17:18:72:540:496:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:equilibria. Section 4 establishes the multiplicityresult and discusses equilibrium dynamics. Section
5:135:10226:18:18:72:540:478:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:5 examines robustness to the introduction of shocks in the fundamentals.  Section 6 introduces
5:136:10320:18:17:72:540:460:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:public news and signals about past attacks. Section 7 concludes. Proofs omitted in the main text
5:137:10416:17:27:72:220:443:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:are presented in the Appendix.
5:138:10446:27:17:91:540:416:120:g_d0_f11:120:g_d0_f4:A:Related Literature.This paper contributes to a small but growing literature on dynamic
5:139:10532:17:18:71:539:399:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:global games. Heidhues and Melissas (2003) identify a condition of dynamic strategic complemen-
5:140:10627:18:17:72:540:381:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:tarity that suffices for uniqueness in an investment model; this condition is also implicit in Gian-
5:141:10727:17:18:72:539:364:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:nitsarou and Toxvaerd’s (2003) uniqueness theorem for recursive binary-action games. Dasgupta
5:142:10820:18:18:72:540:346:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:(2002) examines the role of social learning in a two-period investment model with irreversible ac-
5:143:10918:18:17:72:539:328:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:tions. Levin (2001) considers a global game with overlapping generations of players. Goldstein and
5:144:11016:17:18:72:540:311:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Pauzner (2001) and Goldstein (2002) consider models of contagion. Frankel and Pauzner (2000),
5:145:11109:18:18:72:539:293:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:on the other hand, consider a complete-information dynamic coordination game, where uniqueness
5:146:11203:18:17:72:539:275:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:is obtained by assuming aggregate shocks and idiosyncratic inertia. None of these papers, however,
5:147:11301:17:19:72:407:258:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:examines the role of information dynamics in games of regime change.
5:148:11369:19:17:91:539:239:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Closer to our analysis, Morris and Shin (1999) consider a dynamic model whose stage game
5:149:11457:17:18:72:540:222:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:is similar to ours, but where fundamentals follow a random walk and are commonly observed at
5:150:11549:18:17:72:540:204:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the end of each period.  This reduces the analysis to a sequence of static games with a unique
5:151:11643:17:19:72:129:187:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrium.
5:152:11655:19:18:91:539:168:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:This paper departs from the above literature in that it considers dynamics as a natural source of
5:153:11752:18:17:72:540:150:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:information. In this respect, it shares with Angeletos, Hellwig and Pavan (2003) — which considers
5:154:11850:17:18:72:540:133:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the signaling effects of policy in a static game — the idea thatendogenousinformation structures
5:155:11946:18:17:72:540:115:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:may overturn uniqueness results in global games and lead to predictions that would have not been
5:156:12042:17:19:72:380:98:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:possible with either common knowledge or a unique equilibrium.
5:157:12104:19:0:91:539:79:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Finally, we share with Chari and Kehoe (2003) the motivation that understanding the dynamics
6:158:12197:0:18:72:539:709:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of information may help understand the dynamics of crises. However, whereas they focus on herding,
6:159:12295:18:40:72:322:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:we examine the role of information for coordination.
6:160:12347:40:29:72:325:651:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:C:2  A simple game of regime change
6:161:12380:29:25:72:206:622:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:C:2.1  Static benchmark
6:162:12401:25:18:72:539:597:120:g_d0_f11:120:g_d0_f4:B:Model  set-up.There is a continuum of agents of measure one, indexed byiand uniformly
6:163:12486:18:18:72:539:579:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:distributed over[0,1]. Agents move simultaneously, choosing between two actions: they can either
6:164:12582:18:17:72:526:561:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:attack the status quo (i.e., take an action that favors regime change) or refrain from attacking.
6:165:12679:17:18:91:540:544:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:The payoffstructure is illustrated in Table 1. The payofffrom not attacking(ai=0)is zero,
6:166:12768:18:18:72:542:526:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f12:B:whereas the payofffrom attacking(ai=1)is1−c>0if the status quo is abandoned(R=1)
6:167:12848:18:17:72:540:508:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:and−c<0otherwise(R=0),wherec∈(0,1)parametrizes the relative cost of attacking. An
6:168:12929:17:18:72:540:491:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:agent hencefinds it optimal to attack if and only if he expects regime change with probability at
6:169:13026:18:17:72:540:473:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:leastc. The status quo is in turn abandoned if and only if the measure of agents attacking, which
6:170:13123:17:18:72:539:456:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:we denote byA,is greater than or equal toθ∈R, which parametrizes the strength of the status
6:171:13214:18:18:72:540:438:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:quo. An agent’s incentive to attack thus increases with the aggregate size of attack, implying that
6:172:13313:18:34:72:276:420:120:g_d0_f4:65:g_d0_f4:B:agents’ actions are strategic complements.2
6:173:13356:34:18:245:465:386:120:g_d0_f10:120:g_d0_f12:A:Regime Change(A≥θ)Status Quo(A<θ)
6:174:13389:18:18:138:425:368:120:g_d0_f10:120:g_d0_f6:A:Attack(ai=1)1−c−c
6:175:13406:18:21:138:421:350:120:g_d0_f10:120:g_d0_f12:A:Not Attack(ai=0)00
6:176:13424:21:36:267:344:329:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Table 1. Payoffs
6:177:13440:36:18:91:539:293:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Agents have heterogeneous information about the strength of the status quo. Naturefirst draws
6:178:13533:18:18:72:547:275:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f4:B:θfrom a normal distributionN(z,1/β),which defines the initial common prior aboutθ.Each
6:179:13619:18:17:72:539:257:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:agent then receives a private signalxi=θ+ξi,whereξi∼N(0,1/α)is noise, i.i.d. across agents
6:180:13709:17:18:72:539:240:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:and independent ofθ. The Normality assumptions allow to parametrize the information structure
6:181:13802:18:17:72:539:222:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:parsimoniously with(α, β, z),that is, the precision of private information and the precision and
6:182:13898:17:24:72:202:205:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:mean of the common prior.
6:183:13923:24:18:91:540:181:120:g_d0_f11:120:g_d0_f4:A:Interpretation.Although the game presented above is highly stylized, it admits a variety
6:184:14011:18:18:72:540:163:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of interpretations and possible applications. The most celebrated examples are self-fulfilling bank
6:185:14110:18:17:72:540:145:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:runs, currency attacks, and debt crises. In these contexts, regime change occurs, respectively, when
6:186:14210:17:17:72:540:128:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:a large run forces the banking system to suspend its payments, when a large speculative attack
6:187:14304:17:18:84:542:111:36:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:2Theroleofcoordinationismostevidentwhenθis commonly known by all agents: forθ∈(0,1],thereexisttwo
6:188:14401:18:14:72:539:93:82:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:pure-strategy equilibria, one in which all agents attack and the status quo is abandoned(A=1≥θ)and another in
6:189:14510:14:0:72:354:79:82:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:which no agent attacks and the status quo is maintained(A=0<θ).
7:190:14574:0:18:72:540:709:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:forces the central bank to abandon the peg, or when a country/company fails to coordinate its
7:191:14667:18:17:72:540:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:creditors and is forced to bankruptcy. The model can also be interpreted as one of political change,
7:192:14767:17:18:72:540:674:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:in which a large number of citizens decide whether or not to take actions to subvert a repressive
7:193:14864:18:23:72:296:656:120:g_d0_f4:65:g_d0_f4:B:dictator or some other political establishment.3
7:194:14912:23:18:91:540:633:120:g_d0_f11:120:g_d0_f4:A:Equilibrium analysis.Note that the c.d.f. of an agent’s posterior aboutθis decreasing in
7:195:15000:18:18:72:539:615:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:his private signalx.Moreover, it is strictly dominant to attack for sufficiently low signals – namely
7:196:15101:18:17:72:540:597:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:forx<x,wherexsolvesPr (θ≤0|x)=c– and not to attack for sufficient high signals – namely
7:197:15188:17:18:71:539:580:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:forx> ̄x,where ̄xsolvesPr (θ≤1| ̄x)=c.It is thus natural to look atmonotoneBayesian Nash
7:198:15276:18:17:71:366:562:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:equilibria in which the agents’ strategy is non-increasing inx.

7:206:15686:31:18:72:543:436:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f12:B:The posterior probability of regime change for an agent with signalxis then simplyPr (R=1|x)=

7:209:15923:28:0:215:223:373:120:g_d0_f18:120:g_d0_f18:C:Φ

7:216:15955:28:18:72:540:345:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:A monotone equilibrium is thus identified by a joint solution(ˆx,ˆθ)to (1) and (2). Such a solution
7:217:16054:18:18:72:540:327:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:always exists and is unique for allzifandonlyifα≥β2/(2π).Moreover, iterated elimination of
7:218:16144:18:17:72:539:309:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:strictly dominated strategies implies that, when the monotone equilibrium is unique, there is no
7:219:16240:17:29:72:246:292:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:other equilibrium. We conclude that
7:220:16275:29:18:72:540:263:120:g_d0_f3:120:g_d0_f10:F:Proposition 1 (Static benchmark)In the static game, the equilibrium is unique if and only if
7:221:16367:18:33:72:285:245:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f10:C:α≥β2/(2π),and is in monotone strategies.
7:222:16407:33:25:72:190:212:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:C:2.2  Dynamic game
7:223:16424:25:17:72:540:187:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Wemodifythestaticgamereviewedaboveintwoways:first, we allow agents to attack the status
7:224:16511:17:18:72:417:170:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:quo repeatedly; second, we let agents accumulate information over time.
7:225:16582:18:18:91:540:152:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Time is discrete and indexed byt∈{1,2,...}.The game continues as long as the status quo
7:226:16669:18:17:72:539:134:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:is in place and is over once the status quo is abandoned. We denote withRt=0the event that
7:227:16759:17:18:72:540:117:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the status quo is still in place at the beginning of periodt,withRt=1the alternative event, with
7:228:16855:18:16:71:539:99:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f4:B:ait∈{0,1}the action of agenti,andwithAt∈[0,1]the measure of agents attacking in period
7:229:16941:16:0:84:208:83:36:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:?:3For references, see footnote 1.
8:230:16974:0:18:72:544:709:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f4:B:t. Conditional on the regime being in place at the beginning of periodt(Rt=0),theregimeis
8:231:17063:18:17:72:539:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:abandoned in that period(Rt+1=1)if and only ifAt≥θ,whereθagain represents the strength
8:232:17149:17:31:72:300:674:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of the status quo. Agenti’s payoffin periodtis
8:233:17195:31:30:258:353:643:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f6:A:πit=ait(Rt+1−c),
8:234:17211:30:0:72:281:613:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f12:B:and his payofffrom the entire game isΠi=
8:235:17251:0:11:284:305:621:120:g_d0_f19:65:g_d0_f21:A:P∞
8:236:17253:11:0:296:318:610:65:g_d0_f13:120:g_d0_f6:?:t=1ρ
8:237:17257:0:22:318:540:617:65:g_d0_f13:120:g_d0_f4:A:t−1(1−Rt)πit,whereρ∈(0,1)is the discount
8:238:17297:22:18:72:103:595:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:factor.
8:239:17304:18:18:91:539:577:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Like in the static model,θis drawn at the beginning of the game fromN(z,1/β), which defines
8:240:17395:18:17:72:540:559:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the initial common prior, and never becomes common knowledge. Private information, however,
8:241:17486:17:18:72:539:542:120:g_d0_f4:65:g_d0_f13:B:evolves over time.  In each periodt≥1, every agentireceives a private signal ̃xit=θ+ξit
8:242:17573:18:17:72:540:524:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:aboutθ,whereξit∼N(0,1/ηt)is i.i.d. acrossi, independent ofθ,and serially uncorrelated. Let
8:243:17663:17:18:72:540:507:120:g_d0_f12:120:g_d0_f4:B: ̃xti={ ̃xiτ}tτ=1denote agenti’s history of private signals up to periodt. Individual actions and the
8:244:17764:18:18:71:539:489:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:size of past attacks arenotobservable,4hence the public history in periodtsimply consists of the
8:245:17860:18:17:72:539:471:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:information that the regime is still in place, whereas the private history of an agent is the sequence
8:246:17962:17:0:72:395:454:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f7:B:of own private signals ̃xtiand own past actions. Finally, we letαt≡
8:247:18029:0:12:397:412:462:120:g_d0_f19:65:g_d0_f13:?:Pt
8:248:18031:12:27:409:520:450:65:g_d0_f13:120:g_d0_f4:A:τ=1ητand assume that
8:249:18051:27:30:204:407:423:120:g_d0_f7:120:g_d0_f6:C:∞>αt≥β2/(2π)∀tandlimt→∞αt=∞.
8:250:18079:30:18:72:540:393:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:As shown in the next section,αtparametrizes the precision of private information in periodt.The
8:251:18174:18:17:72:539:375:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:restrictions above ensure equilibrium uniqueness in the static game with precisionαt,and that
8:252:18267:17:26:72:373:358:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:private information becomes infinitely precise only in the limit.
8:253:18332:26:17:91:540:332:120:g_d0_f11:120:g_d0_f4:A:Remark.While this dynamic game is highly stylized, it captures two important dimensions
8:254:18419:17:18:72:540:315:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:that are absent in the static benchmark:first, the possibility of multiple attacks against the status
8:255:18520:18:18:72:540:297:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:quo; and, second, the evolution of beliefs about the probability of regime change. By assuming that
8:256:18619:18:17:72:539:279:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:per-period payoffs do not depend on past or future actions and by ignoring specific institutional
8:257:18716:17:18:72:539:262:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:details, the model may of course fail to capture other interesting effects introduced by dynamics,
8:258:18814:18:17:72:540:244:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:such as, for example, the role of wealth accumulation or liquidity in currency crises.  However,
8:259:18910:17:18:72:539:227:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:abstracting from these other dimensions allows us toisolate information as the driving force for the
8:260:19010:18:25:72:246:209:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:dynamics of coordination and crises.
8:261:19046:25:18:91:539:184:120:g_d0_f11:120:g_d0_f4:A:Equilibrium.In what follows, we limit attention tomonotone equilibria, that is, symmetric
8:262:19135:18:18:71:540:166:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Perfect Bayesian equilibria in which the probability an agent attacks in periodt, which with a slight
8:263:19236:18:17:71:540:148:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:abuseofnotationwedenotewithat( ̃xt), is non-increasing in his private signals ̃xtand independent
8:264:19332:17:18:72:540:131:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of his own past actions.5Restricting attention to this class of equilibria suffices to establish our
8:265:19432:18:18:71:164:113:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:multiplicity results.
8:266:19453:18:12:84:511:95:36:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:?:4The possibility that agents observe noisy signals about aggregate past activity is considered in Section 6.
8:267:19561:12:0:84:529:83:36:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:?:5We donotrestrict the set of available strategies: we look at equilibria in which these properties are satisfied.
9:268:19675:0:29:72:298:709:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:C:3  Equilibrium characterization
9:269:19706:29:18:72:540:680:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Since neither individual nor aggregate actions are observable, andRt=0is always compatible with
9:270:19801:18:17:71:540:662:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:any strategy profile at anyt,6no agent can detect out-of-equilibrium play as long as the status quo
9:271:19900:17:18:72:539:645:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:is in place. It follows that beliefs are pinned down by Bayes’ rule in any relevant history of the game.
9:272:20004:18:18:72:539:627:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Furthermore, payoffs in one period do not depend on own or other players’ actions in any other
9:273:20098:18:17:71:539:609:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:period and hence strategies are sequentially rational if and only if they maximize period-by-period
9:274:20197:17:30:71:298:592:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:payoffs. Finally, definextandαtrecursively by
9:275:20242:30:0:196:218:562:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f12:C:xt=
9:276:20245:0:15:221:242:570:120:g_d0_f6:65:g_d0_f20:?:αt−1
9:277:20249:15:0:227:237:555:120:g_d0_f6:65:g_d0_f13:?:αt
9:278:20251:0:0:244:276:562:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f12:A:xt−1+
9:279:20256:0:15:280:288:570:120:g_d0_f6:65:g_d0_f13:A:ηt

13:481:29039:48:33:72:282:468:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:C:4  Multiplicity and dynamics
13:482:29067:33:17:72:540:435:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Part(v)of Lemma 2 highlights that the arrival of new private information is necessary for further
13:483:29164:17:18:71:540:418:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:attacks to become possible after period 1. Whether this is also sufficient depends on the initial
13:484:29261:18:18:71:539:400:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:prior. This is because an increase in the precisionof private information leads agents to discount,
13:485:29360:18:17:71:539:382:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:not only the information conveyed by the fact that the regime survived past attacks, but also their
13:486:29459:17:20:71:162:365:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:initial prior beliefs.
13:487:29481:20:17:91:539:345:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Whenzis low (“aggressive prior”), an increase in the precision of private information makes
13:488:29572:17:18:71:540:328:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the marginal agent less aggressive in the static game (that is,ˆθtdecreases withαt). The knowledge
13:489:29670:18:18:72:540:310:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:that the regime survived past attacks then only reinforces this effect. Therefore, forzsufficiently
13:490:29769:18:19:72:540:292:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:low, there exists a unique equilibrium and is such that no attack ever occurs after thefirst period.
13:491:29869:19:18:91:540:273:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:When insteadzis high (“lenient prior”), the arrival of new private information makes the
13:492:29957:18:17:72:539:255:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:marginal agent more aggressive, and may eventually offset the incentive not to attack induced by
13:493:30053:17:18:72:539:238:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f6:B:the knowledge that the regime survived past attacks. Indeed, ifzis high enough so thatθ∗1<θ∞,
13:494:30146:18:18:72:540:220:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Lemma 2 ensures that a second attack necessarily becomes possible onceαtis sufficiently high.
13:495:30239:18:17:72:540:202:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Such an example is illustrated in Figure 2. The dashed line represents the payoffof the marginal
13:496:30335:17:18:72:540:185:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:agent in period1.  Its intersection with the horizontal axis definesθ∗1<θ∞.The payoffof the
13:497:30426:18:18:72:540:167:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:marginal agent in period2is represented by the dotted line, and that in period3by the solid line.
13:498:30523:18:17:72:540:149:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:Clearly,α2is low enough that no attack is possible in period2.Incontrast,α3is high enough that
13:499:30617:17:18:72:540:132:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:a new attack is possible. There thus exist at least three equilibria in this example: one in which
13:500:30715:18:17:72:538:114:120:g_d0_f6:65:g_d0_f20:F:θ∗t=θ∗1for allt,another in whichθ∗2=θ∗1andθ∗t=θ03for allt≥3,andathirdinwhichθ∗2=θ∗1
13:501:30798:17:18:72:539:97:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:andθ∗t=θ003for allt≥3,whereθ03andθ003correspond to the two intersections of the solid line with
13:502:30893:18:0:72:164:79:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the horizontal axis.
14:503:30915:0:18:91:540:709:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:In the example of Figure 2, bothθ03andθ003are lower thanθ∞. By Lemma 2, then, a third attack
14:504:31007:18:17:72:539:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:also becomes possible at some future date. More generally, ifzis sufficiently high, any solution
14:505:31103:17:18:72:539:674:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:to (6) is bounded from above byθ∞in all periods, which ensures that a new attack eventually
14:506:31194:18:18:72:539:656:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:becomes possible after any unsuccessful one.  Hence, forzsufficiently high, not only there are
14:507:31288:18:27:72:495:638:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:multiple equilibria, but any arbitrary number of attacks can be sustained in equilibrium.

15:547:34495:18:17:91:539:539:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:In the remainder of this section, we identify equilibrium properties that may turn useful in
15:548:34587:17:28:71:229:522:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:understanding crises phenomena.
15:549:34618:28:18:71:540:494:120:g_d0_f3:120:g_d0_f10:F:Corollary 1Supposeθ>θ∞andz>z.The status quo survives in any equilibrium.  Neverthe-
15:550:34701:18:17:72:540:476:120:g_d0_f10:120:g_d0_f10:F:less,  there existst<∞such that,  at anyt≥t,  an attack is possible,  yet need not take place.
15:551:34795:17:28:72:341:459:120:g_d0_f10:120:g_d0_f10:C:Furthermore, any arbitrarynumber of attacks can occur.
15:552:34849:28:18:91:539:431:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:This seems to square well with the common view that economic fundamentals may help predict
15:553:34939:18:18:72:540:413:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:eventual outcomes (e.g., whether a currency is eventually devalued) but not when a crisis will occur
15:554:35039:18:17:72:540:395:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:or whether attacks will cease. On the contrary, this view is inconsistent with the common-knowledge
15:555:35138:17:18:72:540:378:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:version of the model, in which case fundamentals fail to predict both the timing of attacks and the
15:556:35237:18:18:72:540:360:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:eventual regime outcome,9as well as with unique-equilibrium models like Morris and Shin (1999),
15:557:35332:18:17:72:540:342:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:in which both the timing of attacks and the ultimate fate of the regime are uniquely pinned down
15:558:35428:17:18:72:154:325:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:by fundamentals.
15:559:35444:18:28:91:490:307:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Consider now how the dynamics of attacks depend on the dynamics of information.
15:560:35523:28:17:72:540:279:120:g_d0_f3:120:g_d0_f10:F:Corollary 2After the most aggressive attack for a given period occurs, the game enters a phase
15:561:35617:17:18:72:539:262:120:g_d0_f10:120:g_d0_f10:F:of tranquillity, during which no attack is possible.  This phase is longer the slower the arrival of
15:562:35717:18:28:72:168:244:120:g_d0_f10:120:g_d0_f10:C:private information.
15:563:35737:28:18:91:539:216:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Along with the property that forθ>θ∞andz>za new attack eventually becomes possible
15:564:35819:18:17:72:539:198:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:after any unsuccessful one, the above result implies that dynamics may take the form of cycles in
15:565:35916:17:18:72:539:181:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:which the economy alternates from phases of tranquillity to periods of crisis, eventually resulting
15:566:36015:18:17:72:540:163:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:into a new attack, without any change in the underlying fundamentals. Once again, this would not
15:567:36111:17:49:72:426:146:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:be possible either under common knowledge or with a unique equilibrium.
15:568:36182:49:18:84:539:97:36:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:9Of course, this is true providedθ∈[0,1].If insteadθ/∈[0,1],fundamentals predict both the timing and thefinal
15:569:36291:18:0:72:492:79:82:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f4:F:outcome, as forθ<0it is dominant to attack immediately and forθ>1it is dominant never to attack.
16:570:36389:0:29:72:242:709:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:C:5  Unobservable shocks
16:571:36411:29:17:72:539:680:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:In this section, we examine the possibility that the critical size of attack that triggers regime change
16:572:36515:17:18:72:540:663:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:varies stochastically over time due to unobservable shocks. This is not only a realistic scenario,
16:573:36613:18:17:72:540:645:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:but also an appropriate perturbation. In the model without shocks, the knowledge that the regime
16:574:36709:17:18:72:540:628:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:is in place att≥2makes it common certainty thatθ>0,which explains why there always exist
16:575:36797:18:18:71:539:610:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:equilibria in which nobody attacks att≥2.In contrast, shocks may guarantee that a positive
16:576:36887:18:17:71:539:592:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:measure of agents attack in every period by “smoothing out” the information generated by the
16:577:36979:17:18:71:539:575:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:knowledge that the regime survived past attacks and ensuring the existence of a lower dominance
16:578:37074:18:18:71:179:557:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:region in every period.
16:579:37097:18:17:91:539:539:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:We modify the game as follows. Agents continue to receive private signals aboutθas in the
16:580:37186:17:18:71:543:522:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:benchmark model, but the regime is now abandoned in periodtifandonlyifAt≥θ+δωt,where
16:581:37270:18:17:72:539:504:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f4:B:δ≥0andωtis a real random variable with continuous c.d.f.F,independent ofθand the noise in
16:582:37359:17:18:71:539:487:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the agents’ signals.ωtcan be interpreted as a shock to the fundamentals (i.e., the strength of the
16:583:37457:18:18:71:540:469:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:regime) andδas the volatility of these shocks. Denoting withΓ(δ)the game in which the volatility
16:584:37553:18:23:71:297:451:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f6:B:isδ,the baseline model can be nested asδ=0.
16:585:37596:23:18:91:539:428:120:g_d0_f11:120:g_d0_f4:A:Equilibrium characterization withδ>0.In the presence of shocks, the regime outcome
16:586:37678:18:17:71:540:410:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:depends, not only onθ,but also onωt.As a result, we loose the ability to characterize the set of
16:587:37774:17:18:72:540:393:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:monotone equilibria in terms of a sequence of truncation points forθ. Nevertheless, we can still

16:589:37969:17:18:72:233:358:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f6:B:andonlyifxt≤ ̄xt,where ̄xt∈R.
16:590:37998:18:18:91:539:340:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Considerfirst the regime outcomes induced by a given{ ̄xt}∞t=1.  The size of the attack in

19:868:44409:17:20:72:261:181:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:truncated one of the benchmark model.
19:869:44446:20:18:91:539:161:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:In Figure 4, the solid line represents the payoffV2(x∗1,x2;0)of the marginal agent in period
19:870:44538:18:17:71:540:143:120:g_d0_f12:120:g_d0_f4:B:2forδ=0,whereas the other two lines representV2( ̄x1(δ),x2;δ)forδ>0.12Note that, for
19:871:44622:17:18:72:540:126:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f4:B:x2small enough,V2is negative whenδ=0but positive whenδ>0,which implies that nobody
19:872:44704:18:25:71:540:108:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:attacking in period2is part of an equilibrium in the benchmark model but not in the game with
19:873:44797:25:0:80:540:83:36:g_d0_f4:82:g_d0_f15:F:12In order to illustrateV2over its entire domain, thefigure depictsV2( ̄x1(δ),x2;δ)againstΦ(x2)rather thanx2.
20:874:44908:0:18:72:540:709:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:shocks.13Moreover, whenδis high (dotted line),V2is monotonic inx2and therefore has a single
20:875:44999:18:17:72:540:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:intersection with the horizontal line, in which case the equilibrium would be unique if the game
20:876:45095:17:18:72:539:674:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:endedinperiod2. When, instead,δis sufficiently small (dashed line),V2is non-monotonic and
20:877:45184:18:18:72:540:656:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:has three intersections, which correspond to three different equilibria for the two-period game with
20:878:45284:18:17:72:539:638:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:shocks. Finally, the middle and the highest intersections approximate the two intersections of the
20:879:45382:17:18:72:545:621:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:solid line, while the lowest intersection is arbitrarily small, thus approximatingx∗2=−∞.Along
20:880:45476:18:17:72:539:603:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:with the fact that ̄x1(δ)converges tox∗1,this implies that any equilibrium of the two-period game
20:881:45573:17:19:72:449:586:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:without shocks can be approximated by an equilibrium in the perturbed game.
20:882:45648:19:18:91:539:567:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:In conclusion, what sustains multiplicity in the dynamic game is the non-monotonicity of the
20:883:45740:18:17:72:540:549:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:payoffof the marginal agent generated by the knowledge that the regime survived past attacks.
20:884:45833:17:18:72:539:532:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:That this knowledge resulted in posterior beliefs that assign zero measure to sufficiently lowθin
20:885:45930:18:45:72:255:514:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the benchmark model, is not essential.

22:1048:51465:26:17:72:540:255:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:where1tis an indicator variable that takes value1if an attack occurrs att(At>0)and0otherwise.
22:1049:51558:17:18:91:539:238:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Although the realizations of(xt,zt)and similarly the dynamics of(αt,βt)are now partly
22:1050:51643:18:18:72:540:220:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:endogenous, the equilibrium characterization is otherwise the same as in the model with only
22:1051:51735:18:17:72:540:202:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:exogenous signals. By implication, the multiplicity results extend to the game with signals about
22:1052:51832:17:18:72:540:185:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:past attacks. Similarly, the structure of equilibrium dynamics remains as in the benchmark model,
22:1053:51929:18:18:72:540:167:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:except for the property that an unsuccessful attack does not necessarily reduce the incentives for
22:1054:52027:18:17:72:540:149:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:further attacks. This is because an unsuccessfulattack now also generates new private and public
22:1055:52123:17:18:72:540:132:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:signals, which in some cases may offset the impact of the knowledge that the status quo is still in
22:1056:52222:18:17:71:98:114:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:place.
22:1057:52228:17:18:91:539:97:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:To see this, consider the case where all signals are private(γxt>0,ηxt≥0,γzt=ηzt=0),in
22:1058:52314:18:0:72:539:79:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:which case the only novel effect is that an unsuccessful attack leads to an endogenous increase in
23:1059:52414:0:18:72:539:709:120:g_d0_f6:120:g_d0_f4:B:αt. A further attack is then possible only if this increase is large enough, like in the benchmark
23:1060:52512:18:17:71:546:691:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:game.  On the other hand, when the endogenous signal is public(γzt>0=γxt),anewattack
23:1061:52596:17:18:72:500:674:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:becomes possible if this signal is low enough, like in the case with exogenous public news.
23:1062:52687:18:18:91:539:656:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:We conclude that signals about the size of past attacks may substitute for the exogenous arrival
23:1063:52783:18:39:72:444:638:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of private and/or public information, but do not otherwise affect the analysis.
23:1064:52862:39:28:72:189:599:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:C:7Conclusion
23:1065:52873:28:18:72:540:571:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:This paper examined how the dynamics of information influences the dynamics of coordination in
23:1066:52967:18:17:72:540:553:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:a global game of regime change. We found that dynamics may sustain multiple equilibria under
23:1067:53059:17:18:72:539:536:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:the same informational assumptions that guarantee uniqueness in the static benchmark examined
23:1068:53152:18:18:72:151:518:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:in the literature.
23:1069:53170:18:17:91:539:500:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:A:Although the model is highly stylized and abstracts from all sorts of institutional details and
23:1070:53265:17:18:72:539:483:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:intertemporal payofflinkages, it generates a few distinctivepredictions for equilibrium dynamics,
23:1071:53362:18:17:72:540:465:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:such as the possibility that fundamentals predict regime outcomes but not the timing and number
23:1072:53457:17:18:72:540:448:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:of attacks, or the succession of phases of tranquility, during which agents accumulate information
23:1073:53555:18:18:72:540:430:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:and no attacks are possible, and periods of crises, during which attacks may occur but do no
23:1074:53647:18:17:72:540:412:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:necessarily take place. These predictions may help understand the dynamics of crises phenomena
23:1075:53741:17:18:72:540:395:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:such as currency attacks,financial crashes, or political change. Extending the analysis to these
23:1076:53837:18:89:72:314:377:120:g_d0_f4:120:g_d0_f4:B:applications is a promising line for future research.
23:1077:53890:89:27:72:141:288:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:C:Appendix
